### dimension: checkpoints
Claude SUMMARY: The live DR run path (run_honest_sweep_r3.run_one_query) is STRICTLY FORWARD-ONLY with ZERO stage-level resume. The pipeline stages execute in one monolithic try-block — scope -> retrieval (run_live_retrieval, in-memory LiveRetrievalResult) -> corpus adequacy/approval -> composition (generate_multi_section_report, all sections via asyncio.gather) -> per-sentence strict_verify/NLI -> 4-role D8 seam -> manifest. EVERY durable artifact (report.md L6834, evidence_pool.json L7059, verification_details.json L7025, bibliography.json L6835, manifest.json) is written ONLY AT THE END, after composition succeeds. There is no per-stage persisted snapshot and no resume read on re-run. So the exact failure observed (a section wallclock TimeoutError raised inside the composition gather, multi_section_generator.py:93) propagates to the bare `except Exception` at run_honest_sweep_r3.py:8484, writes a content-free error_unexpected manifest, and DISCARDS everything — the ~3h of retrieval + any completed sections + all verification. Nothing on disk can be reloaded; a re-run re-fetches every URL and re-generates every section from zero. The only on-disk reuse layers are sub-stage accelerators (authority_enrich.sqlite per-source enrich cache in live_retriever; the best-effort retrieval_cache.sqlite cache-warming layer, only warmed for q.canonical_urls and never consulted as a corpus checkpoint) — neither is a stage checkpoint. The sweep loop itself (L8826-8851) calls run_one_query unconditionally

# POLARIS PROJECT - Operational Directives

CRITICAL: This file (CLAUDE.md) MUST be read in its entirety at the start of EVERY session and immediately following ANY restart. Failure to adhere to these directives constitutes a critical operational failure. See §3 for the mandatory startup protocol.

Document Class: Operational, Binding, Project-Specific
Scope: All POLARIS development, research pipeline implementation, and maintenance tasks.

---

## §-1. STANDING EVALUATION & DEBUG STANDARDS (binding for ALL work)

**These three standards override every other directive in this file when they conflict. §-1.1 and §-1.2 were flagged by user 2026-05-09 night as repeat-violation patterns; §-1.3 was operator-locked 2026-06-13 after a full day lost to symptom-patching.**

### §-1.1 Line-by-line audit standard (clinical-safety-critical)

Every evaluation, audit, comparison, benchmark, regression check, BEAT-BOTH framing, or quality assessment **MUST** be:

1. **Claim-by-claim** against the actually-fetched source content (cited span text, not title or abstract).
2. **Reasoning-step-by-reasoning-step** — verify each piece of reasoning follows from the cited evidence.
3. **Citation-by-citation** — verify each citation is appropriate for the claim.
4. **Apply industrial benchmarks** appropriate to the domain:
   - Clinical: PRISMA 2020, AMSTAR-2, GRADE per claim, ICMJE authorship/COI, ICH-GCP for trial methods, Cochrane RoB 2 / ROBINS-I / QUADAS-2.
   - Regulatory: jurisdiction-specific (FDA label, EMA SmPC, Health Canada PM, NICE TA, MHRA AR, TGA PI, PMDA review, NMPA labeling).
   - Methodology: appropriate risk-of-bias tool for the study type.
5. **Both Claude and Codex run independent line-by-line audits in parallel.** Cross-review combines findings.
6. Per-claim verdict: **VERIFIED / PARTIAL / UNSUPPORTED / FABRICATED / UNREACHABLE** with the specific cited span quote that supports the verdict.

**STRICTLY BANNED:**
- Word counts / citation counts / unique-source counts as quality signals
- Pattern presence ("does the report mention 'tirzepatide'?")
- Sample-based audits ("we audited 5 of 50 claims")
- String-presence PASS/FAIL checks (e.g., gate tables)
- Metadata comparison (e.g., "ChatGPT has 27 contradictions, POLARIS has 3, so ChatGPT is better" — this framing is **lethal in clinical context**)

**Why this matters:** clinical context. Pattern-matching evaluation will miss real fabrications. Patients can be hurt by a wrong dose, wrong contraindication, wrong indication population that survived a metadata check. "It is lethal" is literal.

**Application:** when the user asks for an audit/evaluation/comparison/benchmark, line-by-line is the ONLY acceptable answer. If you propose a metadata or pattern audit, you have failed the user.

### §-1.2 Standard debug workflow (no §3.0 bypass)

Every task / bug / issue follows this exact sequence — no shortcuts:

1. **GitHub Issue FIRST.** `gh issue create` BEFORE any branch, any code, any brief. Title format: `I-<prefix>-NNN — <summary>`. Body has acceptance criteria. **No exceptions.**
2. **Comprehensive grep/scan adjacent files.** Before writing the brief, grep all call sites, consumers, downstream rule checks, and tests touching the area. List them in the brief under **"Files I have ALSO checked and they're clean: [...]"**.
3. **Smoke test offline.** Unit tests run; if the change touches the pipeline, run a minimal smoke test (single sentence, single section) BEFORE launching a full sweep. Full sweeps are NOT smoke tests.
4. **Brief Codex.** Open with the iter-1 cap directive (§8.3.1 verbatim). Include the adjacent-file scan results so Codex VERIFIES rather than discovers.
5. **Goal: 1-2 iters per task, not 5.** The 5-cap is a backstop, not a target.
6. **If a big bug surfaces and cannot be resolved in 5 iters, mark it as URGENT new GitHub Issue and resolve it FIRST.** Do not let cap-5 force-approve a real production blocker.
7. **Close the GitHub Issue when the PR merges.** Do not leave resolved issues open.

**Ordering vs §3.1 boot ritual + §3.0 halt gates:** §-1.2 governs *task-work* tool calls. The §3.1 step-0 canonical-pin verification, CHARTER+PLAN SHA pins (§10), halt-marker check (`state/halt_*`), and any active halt gate ALWAYS run first. Only after those pass does the issue-driven sequence below kick in.

**Application:** for the assigned task, the FIRST *task-work* tool call (after boot ritual + halt checks) is `gh issue create` or `gh issue view`. The SECOND is comprehensive grep. The THIRD is offline smoke test. THEN brief Codex. Anything else is a §3.0 violation.

### §-1.3 Deep-research pipeline architecture DNA (operator-locked 2026-06-13)

**The pipeline is WEIGHT-AND-CONSOLIDATE, not FILTER-AND-CAP.** Locked by the operator after a full day was lost to symptom-patching the pipeline with hardcoded caps/targets/thinners to hit a breadth NUMBER. Three binding principles govern every retrieval/selection/composition design decision:

1. **WEIGHT, DON'T FILTER.** Every relevant source flows through to composition carrying a credibility **weight** (peer-review status, journal/venue reputation, gov / institute / news / social media). Do NOT hard-drop a source to hit a number. Social media STAYS at low weight — sometimes it reports a real journal. The tier classifier (T1–T7) and `authority_score` ARE the weighting system: use them as a per-citation **weight surfaced to the user**, never as a rank-then-drop hard filter.

2. **CONSOLIDATE, DON'T DROP.** Group sources that carry the SAME claim into a **basket**. Repetition is **corroboration** — the entire point of consolidate / distill / map-reduce. Multiple citations per claim is GOOD and expected. `finding_dedup` / `fact_dedup` must CONSOLIDATE (keep ALL sources per claim as multi-citation) and operate on **qualitative** claims too — never delete corroborating sources, never restrict to numeric-only.

3. **BASKET FAITHFULNESS.** Decide a claim's faithfulness against its **whole basket** of supporting sources, never a single URL/span — single-source verification is a blind spot. The verdict carries the corroboration (count + weights + agreement). This **STRENGTHENS** faithfulness; it NEVER relaxes it.

**THE ONLY HARD GATE is the faithfulness engine** (strict_verify / NLI entailment / 4-role D8 / provenance / span-grounding). Everything else is a WEIGHT or a CONSOLIDATION — never a DROP / CAP / THIN / TARGET.

**BANNED anti-pattern (the day-waster):** bolting hardcoded caps / targets / thinners / hard-filters onto the pipeline to make a breadth number go up (`PG_SPAN_PER_SOURCE_CITE_CAP`, `PG_LEGACY_SECTION_BREADTH_TARGET`, `PG_BREADTH_CANARY_MIN`, scope hard-filter, and similar). They FIGHT the architecture. Breadth and quality **EMERGE** from honest weighted multi-attribution; they are never forced. If you find yourself adding a knob to make a number hit a target — STOP. That is the bug.

**SURGICAL, NOT REWRITE.** The good machinery already exists — STORM retrieval, Zyte/crawl4ai/distill, the tier classifier (= weighting), `finding_dedup`/`fact_dedup` (= consolidation), the faithfulness engine. RE-WIRE it to the right semantics (weight not filter; consolidate-keep-all not drop; basket not single-span) and DELETE only the specific number-forcing bolt-ons. Do not over-kill.

Canonical detail lives in `docs/polaris_pipeline_canonical.md` and the forensic design doc `docs/pipeline_architecture_forensic_2026_06_13.md`. GitHub anchor: **I-arch-001 (#1245)**.

## §0. Core Identity and Operational Mode

**0.1 Identity:** You operate as a Senior Software Engineer/AI Agent building POLARIS - a production-grade research pipeline. Your responsibility is the high-fidelity implementation of reproducible, fully documented, and production-ready systems.

**0.2 Primary Directive:** Implement the Active Project Definition (APD) as defined in §1.1.
- **Rigor:** Execute without omission, ad-hoc simplification, or corner-cutting. Do not be sloppy. Do not simplify. Do not silently degrade functionality or quality.
- **Exploration:** During exploratory phases where the APD is intentionally broad, the directive is to clarify intent, deliver high-value iterations, and rigorously document findings and the evolution of the scope (LAW I).

**0.3 Operational Mode (Mandatory Extended Thinking):** You must always engage extended thinking capabilities for planning. Every task requires this rigorous process:
1. **Analyze:** Deconstruct the request and synthesize the current APD (§1.1).
2. **Research:** Proactively search online for the latest best practices, libraries, and solutions (LAW III).
3. **Plan:** Formulate a detailed, step-by-step execution plan, considering edge cases and alternatives.
4. **Execute:** Implement the plan rigorously, ensuring synchronization (LAW I).
5. **Verify:** Validate the output against requirements and log the evidence (LAW II).
6. **Record:** Update all mandatory documentation and state files (§2).

The reasoning derived from steps 1-3 MUST be captured in the RATIONALE section of the session log (§2.2).

## §1. The LAWS (Non-Negotiable Directives)

These LAWS supersede all other instructions.

### LAW I — Active Definition and Synchronization
You must adhere strictly to the Active Project Definition (APD) and ensure its components are coherent.

**1.1 Active Project Definition (APD) Hierarchy** (updated 2026-05-05 per polaris-restart Plan §9.1 issue-driven workflow): The APD is the dynamic source of truth for the project's current goals. It is derived, in order of precedence, from:
1. Current Session Instructions: Explicit requests and clarifications made during the active session.
2. `state/active_issue.json` (The Active Work): currently in_progress GitHub Issue per `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md`. Cannot start Issue N+1 until Issue N completed.
3. `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md` (The Scope): 134 issues, Codex APPROVE iter 4 on 2026-05-05. Per-Issue GREEN criteria. Authoritative for what's "done" in issue-driven workflow.
4. `state/polaris_restart/plan.md` (The Restart Plan): Codex APPROVE iter 4. Defines role split, halt conditions, mechanical gates.
5. `docs/carney_delivery_plan_v6_2.md` (The Long-term Mission): canonical 18-week plan, hash-pinned via `docs/canonical_pin.txt`. Re-read at every session-resume.
6. Recent `logs/session_log.md` (The History).
7. `architecture.md` (The Baseline).
8. `docs/task_acceptance_matrix.yaml` (HISTORICAL — Plan-v13-era pre-Issue tracking; matrix-decommission scheduled as post-Cleanup-PR-8 follow-up PR).

**1.2 Mandatory Synchronization:** If a higher-priority item contradicts a lower-priority item, the lower-priority documentation MUST be updated immediately to reflect the higher-priority truth. This synchronization must occur before execution proceeds and must be logged (§2.2).

**1.3 Adherence:** No requirement derived from the synchronized APD may be altered, simplified, or omitted without following the protocols in §6.

### LAW II — No Fake Working (Evidence Required)
- **Forbidden:** Placeholders, mocked data (outside tests/fixtures/), silent downgrades, "demo-only" hacks.
- **Evidence:** Claims of completion require verifiable proof logged in the session log: created files, sizes/counts, checksums, and successful test outputs or key findings.
- **Data & Execution Integrity:**
  - Real Data Only: Use ONLY real data from verified sources. NO synthetic data, NO np.random/faker outside tests/fixtures/.
  - Fail Loudly: If data is unavailable, FAIL LOUDLY; never return empty/default values silently.
  - No Silent Fallbacks: Never silently downgrade capabilities, disable functions, or suppress errors.
  - Stop on Blockers: If a tool/dependency is missing, STOP, report the blocker, and await resolution.
  - Definition of Fixed: Do not mark an issue "fixed" unless you have a reproducible failing test that now passes AND artifacts demonstrating the fix.

### LAW III — Proactive Information Seeking
Do not rely on stale internalized knowledge. You must proactively search the internet for the latest official documentation, best practices, and solutions for every library, API, and function used.
Log all consulted resources in `logs/session_log.md`.

### LAW IV — Persistence of State (Never Forget)
The session must be resumable without loss of context.
Every significant action, decision, or finding must update the durable state files (§2).

### LAW V — Absolute Code and File Hygiene
Adhere strictly to the standards defined in §4 (Naming Conventions, Modularity, and Structure). The repository must remain clean and tidy at all times.

### LAW VI — Zero Hard-Coding
All parameters (endpoints, credentials, thresholds, file paths, batch sizes) must come from configuration files, CLI arguments, or environment variables.
Fixed values for testing must reside exclusively in `tests/fixtures/`.

### LAW VII — CLI Isolation (POLARIS-Specific)
Phases are standalone CLI scripts. They communicate ONLY through JSON files.
- Phase N reads ONLY from `outputs/P{N-1}/{vector_id}.json`
- Phase N writes ONLY to `outputs/P{N}/{vector_id}.json`
- Phase N NEVER imports code from other phases
- Shared utilities go in `src/utils/` or `src/schemas/`

The following files are the authoritative record of the project state. They must be updated continuously with every change, no matter how small.

### 2.1 Authoritative Files (updated 2026-05-05 per polaris-restart Plan §9.5)
- `state/active_issue.json`: **The Active Work.** Currently in_progress GitHub Issue. Read at session boot per §10 ritual. Updated by user assignment (TaskCreate), NOT by Claude advancing autonomously.
- `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md`: **The Scope (issue-driven).** 134 issues, Codex APPROVE iter 4 on 2026-05-05. Per-Issue GREEN criteria.
- `state/polaris_restart/plan.md`: **The Restart Plan.** Codex APPROVE iter 4. Role split, halt conditions, mechanical gates.
- `state/polaris_restart/charter_sha_pin.txt`: SHA pins of `polaris-controls/CHARTER.md` AND `polaris-controls/PLAN.md`. Both verified at every session-resume per §3.1 step 0.
- `state/polaris_restart/cleanup_audit.md`: Codex APPROVE iter 21. 10-PR Cleanup-PR-1..PR-8 sequential schedule.
- `logs/session_log.md`: A chronological, append-only audit trail.
- `docs/task_acceptance_matrix.yaml`: **HISTORICAL** (Plan-v13-era pre-Issue tracking). Matrix-decommission scheduled as post-Cleanup-PR-8 follow-up PR. Do not write new entries here; use `state/active_issue.json` for current issue state.
- `docs/canonical_pin.txt`: SHA256 pin of 10 canonical files; verified at every session-resume per §3 Step 0.
- `logs/bug_log.md`: Registry of defects, blockers, clarification requests, and degradation proposals.
- `docs/file_directory.md`: A hierarchical inventory of all active files, describing the purpose of each.
- `state/restart_instructions.md`: Precise instructions on how to resume the session from the last executed task.
- `state/progress_ledger.jsonl`: Machine-readable append-only execution log for pipeline state.
- `state/last_pointer.json`: Resume point after crash/restart.
- `state/orchestrator_status.json`: Current autoloop heartbeat (current_task, iter, phase).

### 2.2 Session Log Format (MANDATORY)
Every action must be appended to `logs/session_log.md` using this structure:

```
[YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS]
- ACTION: <Brief description of the action taken>
- RATIONALE: <Summary of the extended thinking process (§0.3)>
- DOCS/RESEARCH: <Links to official documentation or resources consulted (LAW III)>
- SYNC: <Description of documentation synchronized due to APD changes (LAW I, §1.2). "N/A" otherwise.>
- AFFECTED_FILES: <List of files read/written/modified>
- EVIDENCE/FINDINGS: <Verifiable output: file sizes, checksums, test results, or key findings (LAW II)>
- STATUS: <Honest assessment of what works, what is incomplete, and any new bugs>
- NEXT_STEP: <The single, clear next action to be taken>
```

## §3.0 Issue-driven workflow (mandatory, per polaris-restart Plan §9.1)

**Every unit of work is a GitHub Issue assigned in sequence per `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md`.** Cannot start Issue N+1 until Issue N is `completed` per TaskCreate state.

**Per-Issue mandatory artifacts** (CI will reject PR without these once PR-D installs the gate workflow; pre-PR-D, this is enforced by Codex review at PR time):
- `.codex/<issue_id>/brief.md` (Claude-authored, Codex-approved)
- `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_brief_verdict.txt` (APPROVE)
- `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_diff.patch` (Claude-written diff committed under this name; Codex reviews it — per plan §7.A LOCKED A2)
- `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_diff_audit.txt` (APPROVE on Red-Team checklist)
- `outputs/audits/<issue_id>/claude_audit.md` (Claude's architect review)
- **`.codex/<issue_id>/codex_visual_audit.txt` — 6th artifact, REQUIRED on PRs touching `web/app/**` or `web/components/**`** (added 2026-05-25 per I-ux-002; AAB pattern per `docs/ui_harness_research_2026_05_25.md`). Generated by `scripts/visual_review_gate.py` against the LOCKED `.codex/visual_audit_rubric.md`. CI gate `codex-visual-required` parses the final `verdict:` line. Non-UI PRs skip cleanly.

**Forbidden patterns:**
- `gh pr merge --admin` from Claude account/token (revoked per CHARTER §1)
- PR opened without all 5 artifacts above
- Issue jump (start `I-X-NNN+1` before `I-X-NNN` merged)
- "While we're at it" polish in same PR
- STATUS block / recap text between PR merge and next branch creation (per §8.2)

**Halt conditions (each emits `state/halt_<utc>_<reason>.md`):**
- canonical pin SHA mismatch
- CHARTER.md OR PLAN.md SHA pin mismatch (per §10 boot ritual + §3.1 step 0)
- issue jump attempt
- PR opened with missing artifact triple
- Codex unavailable >1h
- 2-cycle repeated root cause
- 200-LOC PR cap exceeded
- 3+ PRs queued for user in 24h (reviewer fatigue)

**Role split (per polaris-restart Plan §7.A LOCKED A2 + §7.B LOCKED B1):**
- **Claude:** writes code (briefs AND diffs). Author of `.codex/<issue_id>/brief.md` and `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_diff.patch` (Claude commits the diff, Codex reviews it).
- **Codex:** reviews. Two separate Codex calls per Issue: APPROVE on brief (acceptance criteria correctness) + APPROVE on diff (code correctness against brief). Codex is the only gate.
- **User:** spec owner + merge gate. Reads `git log` in the morning as the after-the-fact human-at-merge surface (B1 pure auto-merge).
- Claude has NO `gh pr merge --admin` authority. CI required check `polaris/codex-required` parses Codex's verdict file and gates merge.

2385:def _abort_if_cancelled(
2386:    q: dict,
2387:    run_dir: Path,
2388:    run_id: str,
2389:    summary: dict,
2390:    log_fn,
2391:) -> bool:
2392:    """I-rdy-011 (#507): cooperative cancel checkpoint for a v6 run.
2393:
2394:    If a cancellation was requested for this v6 run, write a terminal
2395:    `cancelled` manifest, emit the SSE terminal event, mark the summary, and
2396:    return True so run_one_query aborts early at this stage boundary. Returns
2397:    False for non-v6 runs or when no cancel is pending.
2398:
2399:    Best-effort: a run_store lookup failure returns False — a healthy run is
2400:    never aborted on a transient backend hiccup.
2401:    """
2402:    ext = q.get("external_run_id")
2403:    if not (q.get("v6_mode") and ext):
2404:        return False
2405:    try:
2406:        from polaris_v6.queue import run_store
2407:
2408:        if not run_store.is_cancel_requested(ext):
2409:            return False
2410:    except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — cancel-check failure must not abort a healthy run
2411:        return False
2412:    log_fn("[cancel]      cancellation requested — aborting run cooperatively")
2413:    manifest = {
2414:        "run_id": run_id,
2415:        "slug": q.get("slug", ""),
2416:        "domain": q.get("domain", ""),
2417:        "question": q.get("question", ""),
2418:        "status": "cancelled",
2419:    }
2420:    manifest = _attach_tool_utilization(manifest, run_dir)
2421:    (run_dir / "manifest.json").write_text(
2422:        json.dumps(manifest, indent=2, sort_keys=True) + "\n", encoding="utf-8"
2423:    )
2424:    emit_event(ext, "run.completed", {"status": "cancelled"})
2425:    summary["status"] = "cancelled"
2426:    return True

2429:def _normalize_quantified_telemetry(telemetry: dict) -> dict:
2430:    """Add a normalized ``fired`` boolean to the Phase-7 quantified telemetry (I-meta-008 P1-3,
2431:    #1018) so a post-run assertion can detect a SILENT no-op.
2432:
2433:    The quantified block intentionally NEVER aborts the run (broad ``except`` in run_one_query), so
2434:    an error or ``spec_produced=False`` would otherwise leave the manifest carrying the raw
2435:    telemetry but no single clear "did the differentiator actually run" signal. ``fired`` is True
2436:    iff the section produced at least one verified quantified sentence. Idempotent (``setdefault``).
2437:    """
2438:    telemetry.setdefault("fired", int(telemetry.get("verified_sentences", 0) or 0) > 0)
2439:    return telemetry

2441:
2442:def _judge_calls_and_errors_from_telemetry(
2443:    base_tel: dict, now_tel: dict,
2444:) -> tuple[int, int]:
2445:    """FX-09 (I-ready-017): (judge_calls, judge_errors) for THIS run, as the delta of the
2446:    process-lifetime entailment-judge telemetry counters.
2447:
2448:    denominator = actual judge invocations this run (calls delta); numerator = judge_error
2449:    delta (counts errors even on KEPT sentences that failed open). Pure + reentrant: the
2450:    sweep snapshots `base` at the run boundary and never resets the global counters.
2451:    """
2452:    calls = int(now_tel.get("calls", 0)) - int(base_tel.get("calls", 0))
2453:    errors = int(now_tel.get("judge_error", 0)) - int(base_tel.get("judge_error", 0))
2454:    return calls, errors

2457:async def run_one_query(
2458:    q: dict,
2459:    out_root: Path,
2460:    *,
2461:    four_role_transport=None,
2462:    four_role_inputs=None,
2463:    four_role_input_builder=None,
2464:    query_index: int | None = None,
2465:    query_total: int | None = None,
2466:) -> dict:
2467:    """Run the full honest pipeline on one query. Returns a summary dict.
2468:
2469:    I-meta-002 sub-PR-6 (4-role wiring, GUARDED + default OFF): the 4-role evaluation path
2470:    activates ONLY when BOTH ``four_role_transport`` is supplied (an explicit, INJECTED
2471:    ``RoleTransport`` — there is NO default real transport; live transport is Gate-B after lock
2472:    promotion) AND ``PG_FOUR_ROLE_MODE`` is enabled (env "1"/"true"/"True"). When OFF (the
2473:    default), the legacy evaluator-gate path below is byte-unchanged. ``four_role_inputs`` is the
2474:    caller-supplied ``FourRoleEvaluationInputs`` (claims with EXISTING ids, the canonical
2475:    required-element coverage ledger, and the required-S0 set) — the sweep NEVER synthesizes
2476:    them from the report (that extraction is Gate-B). When the branch fires it delegates entirely
2477:    to ``sweep_integration.run_four_role_seam`` (D8 is the single binding gate) and
2478:    overrides BOTH ``manifest['release_allowed']`` AND ``manifest['status']`` from the D8
2479:    decision, demoting the legacy evaluator_gate to ADVISORY metadata only.
2480:
2481:    I-meta-002 PR-9/M3b (Gate-B wiring): ``four_role_input_builder`` is an OPTIONAL no-argument
2482:    closure (wired by ``scripts/dr_benchmark/run_gate_b.py`` over the native
2483:    ``build_native_gate_b_inputs`` + evidence normalization). When supplied it WINS over a
2484:    static ``four_role_inputs``: it is called AFTER generation to PRODUCE the inputs+audit
2485:    bundle, and the seam writes the per-claim audit map to ``four_role_claim_audit.json`` next
2486:    to the run. The default (both None while the branch is OFF) leaves the legacy path
2487:    byte-unchanged.
2488:    """
2489:    reset_run_cost()
2490:    # FX-09 (I-ready-017): begin a per-RUN, concurrency-ISOLATED judge counter so
2491:    # judge_error_rate's denominator is THIS run's ACTUAL judge invocations, not all
2492:    # verifier-checked sentences (the judge only runs on sentences that pass every
2493:    # mechanical check first → the old denominator diluted the #1071 binding
2494:    # abort_verifier_degraded gate ~2.87x). The counter is a contextvar scope, isolated
2495:    # per OS-thread AND per asyncio Task, so a sibling run sharing the process (the v6
2496:    # Dramatiq worker runs `asyncio.run(run_one_query)` under `--threads 2`) cannot
2497:    # contaminate it. Read directly at the rate computation (no process-global delta).
2498:    try:
2499:        from src.polaris_graph.llm.entailment_judge import (
2500:            begin_run_judge_telemetry as _begin_run_judge_telemetry,
2501:        )
2502:        _run_judge_tel = _begin_run_judge_telemetry()
2503:    except Exception:
2504:        _run_judge_tel = None
2505:    # I-bug-111: reset synthesis-scrub alert + telemetry at run
2506:    # boundary so per-run manifest reflects ONLY this run's
2507:    # synthesis behavior. Without this reset, the sticky alert from
2508:    # query N leaks into query N+1's manifest. Defensive lazy
2509:    # import: tolerate environments where the module isn't loaded.
2510:    try:
2511:        from src.polaris_graph.generator.analyst_synthesis import (
2512:            reset_synthesis_scrub_alert,
2513:            reset_synthesis_telemetry,
2514:        )
2515:        reset_synthesis_scrub_alert()
2516:        reset_synthesis_telemetry()
2517:    except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — defensive: alert reset failure must not abort run
2518:        pass
2519:
2520:    # I-pipe-015 (#1240, Codex iter-1 REQUEST_CHANGES): reset the MODULE-GLOBAL token-honesty
2521:    # counters (malformed_canonicalized / malformed_dropped) at the run boundary so they reflect
2522:    # ONLY this query — without this reset they accumulate across queries in a multi-query sweep
2523:    # and the per-run manifest over-reports. Safe regardless of PG_PROVENANCE_TOKEN_HONEST_DROP:
2524:    # when the honest-drop path is off the counters stay 0, so reset/snapshot are no-ops. The
2525:    # snapshot into manifest['token_honesty'] happens at report assembly. Best-effort import.
2526:    try:
2527:        reset_token_honesty_telemetry()
2528:    except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — telemetry reset must never abort the run
2529:        pass

3108:                # `run_one_query` is async — the sweep event loop is already
3109:                # running here — so the coroutine is driven on a SEPARATE
3110:                # thread with its own loop (thread-safe; never touches the
3111:                # running loop, which `run_until_complete` would crash on).
3112:                #
3113:                # I-meta-005 Phase 1 FIX 3 (Codex diff-gate iter-1 P1 #3): the
3114:                # prior bare `ThreadPoolExecutor(...).submit(asyncio.run, ...)`
3115:                # ran with the worker's OWN empty ContextVar state, so the
3116:                # planner Writer call's billed cost accumulated in
3117:                # `_RUN_COST_CTX` only inside the worker snapshot and was LOST
3118:                # to the parent run (`current_run_cost()` / `manifest.cost_usd`
3119:                # under-reported live planner spend — a budget-cap integrity
3120:                # LAW violation). Fix mirrors `auto_induction.llm_inductor`
3121:                # rounds 3-4 (and `scope_classifier_llm._run_async_in_isolated_
3122:                # thread`): capture the parent context with
3123:                # `contextvars.copy_context()` and run the worker inside that
3124:                # snapshot via `parent_ctx.run()` (READ visibility), THEN apply
3125:                # the worker's cost delta back to the parent context via a
3126:                # closure-shared holder (write-back, fires whether or not the
3127:                # call raised — the OpenRouter client bills partial cost before
3128:                # raising on empty-content/retry).
3129:                import asyncio as _asyncio
3130:                import concurrent.futures as _futures
3131:                import contextvars as _contextvars
3132:                from src.polaris_graph.llm.openrouter_client import (
3133:                    _RUN_COST_CTX,
3134:                )
3135:
3136:                _parent_cost_before = _RUN_COST_CTX.get()
3137:                _worker_cost_after_holder: list[float] = [_parent_cost_before]
3138:
3139:                async def _run() -> str:
3140:                    _client = OpenRouterClient(model=PG_GENERATOR_MODEL)
3141:                    try:
3142:                        _resp = await _client.generate(
3143:                            prompt=prompt, max_tokens=2000, temperature=0.2,
3144:                        )
3145:                        return (_resp.content or "").strip()
3146:                    finally:
3147:                        # Capture the worker snapshot's accumulated cost even
3148:                        # on raise (OpenRouter bills partial cost before
3149:                        # raising on empty-content/retry paths).
3150:                        _worker_cost_after_holder[0] = _RUN_COST_CTX.get()
3151:                        if hasattr(_client, "close"):
3152:                            try:
3153:                                await _client.close()
3154:                            except Exception:
3155:                                pass
3156:
3157:                _parent_ctx = _contextvars.copy_context()
3158:
3159:                def _worker() -> str:
3160:                    def _run_under_ctx() -> str:
3161:                        return _asyncio.run(_run())
3162:                    return _parent_ctx.run(_run_under_ctx)
3163:
3164:                try:
3165:                    with _futures.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=1) as _pool:
3166:                        return _pool.submit(_worker).result()
3167:                finally:
3168:                    # Apply the worker's cost delta to the parent context so
3169:                    # the planner Writer spend merges into the parent run cost
3170:                    # (whether or not the worker raised).
3171:                    _cost_delta = (
3172:                        _worker_cost_after_holder[0] - _parent_cost_before
3173:                    )
3174:                    if _cost_delta > 0:
3175:                        _RUN_COST_CTX.set(_parent_cost_before + _cost_delta)

180:    NATIVE-ONLY: nothing here reads the gold rubric.
181:    """

184:        *,

7872:                                        "marker": _ac.marker,
7873:                                    }
7874:                                    for _ac in _annotation.annotated
7875:                                },
7876:                                indent=2,
7877:                                sort_keys=True,
7878:                            )
7879:                            + "\n",
7880:                            encoding="utf-8",
7881:                        )
7882:                        manifest["report_annotation"] = {
7883:                            "annotated_count": _annotation.annotated_count,
7884:                            "annotated_claim_ids": [
7885:                                _ac.claim_id for _ac in _annotation.annotated
7886:                            ],
7887:                            "already_absent_claim_ids": _annotation.already_absent,
7888:                        }
7889:                        _log(
7890:                            "[label]       keep+label report.md vs 4-role verdicts: "
7891:                            f"labeled={_annotation.annotated_count} "
7892:                            f"already_absent={len(_annotation.already_absent)} "
7893:                            "(always-release; non-VERIFIED kept + labeled, never deleted)"
7894:                        )
7895:                else:
7896:                    _audit_map = json.loads(
7897:                        _audit_map_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
7898:                    )
7899:                    try:
7900:                        _redaction = reconcile_report_against_verdicts(
7901:                            _redact_report_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8"),
7902:                            _final_verdicts,
7903:                            _audit_map,
7904:                        )
7905:                    except ReportRedactionError as _redact_exc:
7906:                        # Present-but-unlocatable material claim, or a non-VERIFIED verdict with
7907:                        # no audit row. Do NOT ship the report; take a terminal abort. The
7908:                        # unredacted report.md stays on disk for the curator to inspect.

7915:                            f"[redact]      FAIL-CLOSED: {_redact_exc} -> "
7916:                            "abort_report_redaction_failed"
7917:                        )

7920:                        # reflects the redacted report. Emit one redacted_unsupported gap per
7921:                        # removed claim into gaps.json (append; never overwrite curator gaps).

7929:                                refilter_key_findings_block,

7932:                                _reconciled_report
7933:                            )

7935:                            _reconciled_report, encoding="utf-8"
7936:                        )
7937:                        manifest["report_redaction"] = {
7938:                            "redacted_count": _redaction.redacted_count,
7939:                            "redacted_claim_ids": [
7940:                                rc.claim_id for rc in _redaction.redacted
7941:                            ],
7942:                            "already_absent_claim_ids": _redaction.already_absent,
7943:                        }

7959:                                encoding="utf-8",
7960:                            )

7962:                            f"[redact]      reconciled report.md vs 4-role verdicts: "
7963:                            f"redacted={_redaction.redacted_count} "

2:Multi-section generator — HONEST-REBUILD Gap-4.
3:
4:Three-stage architecture that produces 1500-3000-word reports while
5:keeping per-section provenance tightness:
6:
7:  1. OUTLINE stage  (1 LLM call, ~500 tokens)
8:     DeepSeek reads all evidence and emits a JSON section plan:
9:       [{"title": "Efficacy", "focus": "...", "ev_ids": ["ev_001", ...]},
10:        {"title": "Safety", "focus": "...", "ev_ids": [...]},
11:        {"title": "Comparative", ...}]
12:     Sections constrained to a fixed allowed set so the model can't
13:     invent topics unsupported by evidence.
14:
15:  2. PER-SECTION GENERATION  (N parallel LLM calls, ~800 tokens each)
16:     Each section gets its own prompt with ONLY its evidence subset +
17:     focus statement. Generates 8-15 sentences with [ev_XXX] markers.
18:
19:  3. VERIFY + OPTIONAL REGEN  (deterministic + 0-N retry calls)
20:     Each section is strict_verified. If <50% sentences kept, the
21:     section is regenerated ONCE with a "tighter citations required"
22:     reminder. If regen still fails, the section is dropped (with a
23:     note in the report).
24:
25:  4. ASSEMBLY
26:     verified_sections + shared Methods + contradictions + Limitations
27:     + bibliography, concatenated.
28:
29:Cost estimate: ~$0.01-$0.02 per report (vs $0.0022 for single-call).

57:# I-arch-002 (#1248): per-section wall-clock guard. DEFAULT-OFF
58:# (PG_SECTION_WALLCLOCK_SECONDS unset / <= 0) => byte-identical (no wait_for wrap).
59:# When set, each section's bounded runner is wrapped in asyncio.wait_for so a WEDGED
60:# section (a 0-socket provider stall — observed on the drb_72 smoke: the section
61:# asyncio.gather hung 19 min with NO open sockets / ~0 CPU, immune to the httpx read
62:# timeout because no socket was open to time out) gets a hard wall-clock bound: it
63:# RETRIES once (a fresh call likely hits a healthy provider), then FAILS LOUD instead
64:# of hanging the whole report forever. Faithfulness-neutral: only affects WHETHER a
65:# section generates; strict_verify / NLI / 4-role / provenance are untouched.
66:def _section_wallclock_seconds() -> int:
67:    try:
68:        return int(os.getenv("PG_SECTION_WALLCLOCK_SECONDS", "0"))
69:    except ValueError:
70:        return 0
71:
72:
73:async def _run_section_with_wallclock(runner, plan):
74:    """Wrap a section bounded-runner in a per-section wall-clock guard (I-arch-002
75:    #1248). OFF (<= 0) => exact ``await runner(plan)`` (byte-identical). ON => one
76:    wait_for, one retry, then fail-loud on a persistent wedge. ``runner`` re-runs the
77:    full section on retry (re-acquires the semaphore + re-does the work); a cancelled
78:    first attempt appends nothing, so there is no double-write."""
79:    wall = _section_wallclock_seconds()
80:    if wall <= 0:
81:        return await runner(plan)
82:    last_exc: BaseException | None = None
83:    for attempt in (1, 2):
84:        try:
85:            return await asyncio.wait_for(runner(plan), timeout=wall)
86:        except asyncio.TimeoutError as exc:
87:            last_exc = exc
88:            logger.warning(
89:                "[gen-wallclock] section exceeded %ds wall-clock (attempt %d/2) — "
90:                "likely a transient provider stall; %s",
91:                wall, attempt, "retrying" if attempt == 1 else "failing loud",
92:            )
93:    raise TimeoutError(
94:        f"section generation exceeded {wall}s wall-clock x2 — failing loud instead "
95:        f"of hanging the report (I-arch-002 #1248)"
96:    ) from last_exc

106:# budget against the real 1M-context model — sources flow to composition bounded by
107:# the prompt budget + the faithfulness gate, never by a row count (the DNA: WEIGHT-
108:# AND-CONSOLIDATE, not FILTER-AND-CAP). Faithfulness (strict_verify / NLI / 4-role) is
109:# downstream of full-pool text resolution and is untouched.

277:# FX-17 (#1126): Serper `num` is a PAGE size (provider max ~20); large result sets need the `page`
278:# param (pagination). The old code silently floored `num` to 20 with no warning and never paginated.
279:_SERPER_PAGE_MAX = 20

281:
282:def _serper_fetch_page(
283:    query: str, per_page: int, page: int, headers: dict[str, str]
284:) -> tuple[list[dict[str, Any]], bool, float, int, str]:
285:    """FX-17 (#1126): fetch ONE Serper page. Returns (items, ok, latency_ms, resp_bytes, error).
286:    Byte-identical to the legacy single call when page==1 (no `page` key in the payload)."""
287:    payload: dict[str, Any] = {"q": query, "num": per_page}
288:    if page > 1:
289:        payload["page"] = page
290:    _t0 = time.time()
291:    try:
292:        with httpx.Client(timeout=DEFAULT_HTTP_TIMEOUT) as c:
293:            r = c.post(SERPER_ENDPOINT, json=payload, headers=headers)
294:        _latency_ms = (time.time() - _t0) * 1000.0
295:        if r.status_code != 200:
296:            return [], False, _latency_ms, _resp_content_len(r), f"HTTP {r.status_code}"
297:        organic = (r.json().get("organic", []) or [])
298:        items = [
299:            {"url": it.get("link", ""), "title": it.get("title", ""),
300:             "snippet": it.get("snippet", ""), "source": "serper"}
301:            for it in organic
302:        ]
303:        return items, True, _latency_ms, _resp_content_len(r), ""
304:    except Exception as exc:
305:        return [], False, (time.time() - _t0) * 1000.0, 0, str(exc)

308:def _serper_search(
309:    query: str, num: int = 10, api_calls: dict[str, int] | None = None
310:) -> list[dict[str, Any]]:
311:    api_key = os.getenv("SERPER_API_KEY", "").strip()
312:    if not api_key:
313:        logger.warning("[live_retriever] SERPER_API_KEY missing — skipping Serper")
314:        return []
315:    # I-safety-002b (#925) PR-2: record that the Path-B-required backend was actually
316:    # invoked (key present + call attempted). assert_post_run rejects a run where a
317:    # required backend was never tried. Lazy + best-effort; no-op when gate is off.
318:    try:
319:        from src.polaris_graph.benchmark import pathB_capture as _pathb
320:        _pathb.record_retrieval_attempt("serper")
321:    except Exception:
322:        pass
323:    headers = {"X-API-KEY": api_key, "Content-Type": "application/json"}
324:    per_page = max(1, min(num, _SERPER_PAGE_MAX))
325:    # FX-17 (#1126): make the silent clamp VISIBLE — the inert PG_SWEEP_MAX_SERPER=100 used to floor
326:    # to 20 with no signal. Surface it loudly so the requested-vs-served gap stops lying.
327:    _clamped = num > _SERPER_PAGE_MAX
328:    if _clamped:
329:        logger.warning(
330:            "[live_retriever] Serper num=%d exceeds the page max %d — clamping per-page to %d and "
331:            "paginating to the PG_SERPER_TOTAL_PER_QUERY budget.", num, _SERPER_PAGE_MAX, per_page,
332:        )
333:    # FX-17 (#1126): total-URL budget across pages. DEFAULT = one page (per_page) -> byte-identical to
334:    # the legacy single call; the benchmark slate raises PG_SERPER_TOTAL_PER_QUERY. Page count is
335:    # bounded by PG_SERPER_MAX_PAGES (small) and early-stops when a page returns < per_page.
336:    try:
337:        _total = max(per_page, int(os.getenv("PG_SERPER_TOTAL_PER_QUERY", str(per_page))))
338:    except ValueError:
339:        _total = per_page
340:    try:
341:        _max_pages = max(1, int(os.getenv("PG_SERPER_MAX_PAGES", "3")))
342:    except ValueError:
343:        _max_pages = 3
344:    _n_pages = min(_max_pages, -(-_total // per_page))  # ceil(total/per_page)
345:
346:    # BB-002 (I-beatboth-fix-000 #1171): a sub-`per_page` page-1 count is NOT a reliable
347:    # end-of-results signal for an OFFSET-paginated SERP API — Serper routinely returns
348:    # 10 organic on page 1 even when page 2 has more, so the legacy `len(items) < per_page`
349:    # break short-circuited before page 2 and the PG_SERPER_TOTAL_PER_QUERY budget was never
350:    # reached (de-facto 10/query ceiling — chokepoint #4). When PG_SERPER_STOP_ON_ZERO_NEW=1
351:    # the loop keeps offset-paging until (a) budget met, (b) a page returns 0 NEW (post-dedup)
352:    # items, or (c) PG_SERPER_MAX_PAGES — the only RELIABLE end-of-results signals. DEFAULT OFF
353:    # = byte-identical (the legacy short-page break is preserved). Discovery-breadth only; every
354:    # new URL flows through the same fetch -> strict_verify -> 4-role chokepoint unchanged.
355:    _stop_on_zero_new = os.getenv("PG_SERPER_STOP_ON_ZERO_NEW", "0").strip() in (
356:        "1", "true", "True",
357:    )
358:
359:    out: list[dict[str, Any]] = []
360:    seen: set[str] = set()
361:    _pages_fetched = 0
362:    _last_latency = 0.0
363:    _last_bytes = 0
364:    _last_err = ""
365:    for _page in range(1, _n_pages + 1):
366:        items, ok, _last_latency, _last_bytes, _last_err = _serper_fetch_page(
367:            query, per_page, _page, headers
368:        )
369:        # FX-17 (#1126) iter-2: count EACH HTTP page request (a real Serper API call), not once
370:        # per query. P2 fix — api_calls['serper'] used to undercount paginated breadth.
371:        if api_calls is not None:
372:            api_calls["serper"] = api_calls.get("serper", 0) + 1
373:        if not ok:
374:            _trace_tool(
375:                "serper", target=query, status="fail", latency_ms=_last_latency,
376:                bytes_sent=len(query), bytes_received=_last_bytes,
377:                backend_used="serper_api_v1", error=_last_err, page=_page,
378:            )
379:            logger.warning("[live_retriever] Serper page %d failed for %r: %s",
380:                           _page, query[:60], _last_err)
381:            break  # fail-open: keep pages already accumulated; do not discard.
382:        _pages_fetched += 1
383:        _new = 0
384:        for it in items:
385:            u = it.get("url", "")
386:            if u and u not in seen:
387:                seen.add(u)
388:                out.append(it)
389:                _new += 1
390:        if len(out) >= _total:
391:            break  # budget met.
392:        if _stop_on_zero_new:
393:            # BB-002 (#1171): keep paging past a short page; stop only when a page
394:            # added 0 NEW (post-dedup) URLs — the reliable end-of-results signal.
395:            if _new == 0:
396:                break
397:        elif len(items) < per_page:
398:            break  # legacy (default OFF): short page -> assume no more results.
399:    _trace_tool(
400:        "serper", target=query, status="ok" if out or not _last_err else "fail",
401:        latency_ms=_last_latency, bytes_sent=len(query), bytes_received=_last_bytes,
402:        backend_used="serper_api_v1", result_count=len(out),
403:        pages_fetched=_pages_fetched, num_requested=num, per_page=per_page,
404:        page_max=_SERPER_PAGE_MAX, clamped=_clamped, total_budget=_total,
405:        stop_on_zero_new=_stop_on_zero_new,   # BB-002 (#1171): which stop policy ran
406:    )
407:    _trace_query("serper", query, [o["url"] for o in out])
408:    return out

871:def _authority_cache_init() -> None:
872:    """Create the authority-enrich cache with a VERSIONED migration (C5).
873:
874:    Not a CREATE-IF-NOT-EXISTS no-op: a stale cache whose recorded schema
875:    version is older than AUTHORITY_CACHE_SCHEMA_VERSION is rebuilt rather than
876:    silently used with missing columns.
877:    """
878:    AUTHORITY_CACHE_DB.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
879:    conn = sqlite3.connect(AUTHORITY_CACHE_DB)
880:    try:
881:        conn.execute(
882:            "CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS schema_meta ("
883:            " id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY CHECK (id = 1), version INTEGER NOT NULL)"
884:        )
885:        row = conn.execute("SELECT version FROM schema_meta WHERE id = 1").fetchone()
886:        existing = row[0] if row else 0
887:        table_present = conn.execute(
888:            "SELECT name FROM sqlite_master WHERE type='table' AND name='authority_enrich'"
889:        ).fetchone() is not None
890:        # Migrate whenever the recorded version is older than the current one
891:        # (existing=0 means an unversioned/legacy cache). Drop + rebuild the
892:        # payload table (the cache is a rebuildable accelerator, never the
893:        # source of truth) — NOT a CREATE-IF-NOT-EXISTS no-op (C5).
894:        if table_present and existing < AUTHORITY_CACHE_SCHEMA_VERSION:
895:            conn.execute("DROP TABLE IF EXISTS authority_enrich")
896:            logger.warning(
897:                "[live_retriever] authority cache schema %d < %d — migrating "
898:                "(rebuild)", existing, AUTHORITY_CACHE_SCHEMA_VERSION,
899:            )
900:        conn.execute(
901:            "CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS authority_enrich ("
902:            " key TEXT PRIMARY KEY,"
903:            " payload_json TEXT NOT NULL,"
904:            " fetched_at TEXT DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP)"
905:        )
906:        conn.execute(
907:            "INSERT INTO schema_meta (id, version) VALUES (1, ?)"
908:            " ON CONFLICT(id) DO UPDATE SET version = excluded.version",
909:            (AUTHORITY_CACHE_SCHEMA_VERSION,),
910:        )
911:        conn.commit()
912:    finally:
913:        conn.close()
914:
915:
916:# I-ready-017 #1134 (Codex diff-gate P1): run the versioned migration once before
917:# the FIRST cache access (read OR write), so a stale v1 payload — which predates

src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py:1660:12. **Primary-study framing (M-32, for claim-frame rigor)**: When you name a primary study, trial, cohort, experiment, or any individually identifiable empirical data source, and the cited evidence rows contain the structured metadata, provide the study's FULL FRAME in the FIRST sentence that introduces it: (a) sample size or cohort size (e.g. N=1879), (b) baseline value of the outcome being discussed (e.g. mean baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[VALUE], baseline [SECONDARY_METRIC]=[VALUE]), (c) comparator / control / background condition (e.g. versus [COMPARATOR], versus placebo on [BACKGROUND], versus standard [REFERENCE_CONDITION]), and (d) the primary endpoint + timepoint (e.g. [ENDPOINT] change at [TIMEPOINT], [N-YEAR] [OUTCOME_TYPE], cycle-life to [THRESHOLD] retention). If the evidence row carries this structured metadata, you MUST emit it in that first sentence — do not compress N/baseline/endpoint into a single percent-reduction when the evidence carries the full frame. This is what distinguishes a research-grade deep synthesis from a news-style summary. Example template: "In [STUDY NAME], [STUDY_DESIGN_SUMMARY] randomized N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] participants with baseline [OUTCOME]=[BASELINE_VALUE] to [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR]; [PRIMARY_ENDPOINT] at [TIMEPOINT] was [RESULT] [ev_X]." Subsequent sentences about the same study may reference it by short name without re-framing. Generalizable beyond clinical: a materials paper gets composition + baseline performance + test condition + measured outcome; a cohort study gets population + baseline metric + intervention + outcome; a financial filing gets period + baseline metric + policy/benchmark + reported outcome.

636:def plan_research(
637:    question: str,
638:    *,
639:    planner_llm: Callable[[str], str],
640:    max_subqueries: int = DEFAULT_MAX_SUBQUERIES,
641:    min_subqueries: int = MIN_SUBQUERIES,
642:) -> ResearchPlan:
643:    """Produce a `ResearchPlan` from `question` using ONE Writer call (plus at
644:    most one bounded lower-bound retry).
645:
646:    Args:
647:        question: The raw research question (stored verbatim on the plan).
648:        planner_llm: Injected Writer callable `prompt -> response_text`. This
649:            is the ONLY way the planner reaches an LLM; the module never
650:            constructs an `OpenRouterClient` or a live HTTP client. Tests pass
651:            a fake; production passes the real Writer.
652:        max_subqueries: UPPER bound; >this is merged/truncated deterministically.
653:        min_subqueries: LOWER bound that triggers ONE fail-loud retry.
654:
655:    Returns:
656:        A validated `ResearchPlan` (frame + sub_queries + archetype outline).
657:
658:    Raises:
659:        ValueError: empty question.
660:        PlannerError: malformed / unusable planner output (LAW II — no silent
661:            fallback to the clause-splitter).
662:    """
663:    if not question or not question.strip():
664:        raise ValueError("question must be non-empty.")
665:    if not callable(planner_llm):
666:        raise TypeError("planner_llm must be a callable[[str], str].")
667:
668:    prompt = _build_prompt(
669:        question, more_facets=False, min_subqueries=min_subqueries,
670:    )
671:    raw = planner_llm(prompt)
672:    plan = _parse_plan(raw, question.strip())
673:    plan.sub_queries = _merge_truncate_subqueries(
674:        plan.sub_queries, max_subqueries=max_subqueries,
675:    )
676:
677:    # LOWER-bound policy (brief §2.1): a fail-loud retry, NOT padding. If the
678:    # honest count is short, ask once for more facets. If still short, accept
679:    # the honest smaller count for a genuinely narrow question and log.

692:            retry_plan.sub_queries, max_subqueries=max_subqueries,
693:        )

695:        if len(retry_plan.sub_queries) > len(plan.sub_queries):

425:# sweep is imported so import-time module constants (caps/timeouts) also see the full values.
426:_FULL_CAPABILITY_BENCHMARK_SLATE: dict[str, str] = {
427:    # I-fetch-002 (#1168): the WHOLE run fetches ~1000 sites TOTAL per question, NOT 1000 + additive
428:    # lanes. The operator's ~1000 budget is SPLIT across the four real fetch lanes so they SUM to ~1000
429:    # (the prior 1000 here was the MAIN lane alone, on top of which agentic/deepener/R-6 each added more
430:    # — silently overshooting the budget). The four lanes, FLOOR-applied below (max(existing, slate)):
431:    #   PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP            740  main Serper/S2/OpenAlex lane (total URLs after dedup, /query)
432:    #   PG_AGENTIC_BENCHMARK_URL_CAP  100  agentic-discovery harvest (run_honest_sweep_r3.py:3162)
433:    #   PG_SWEEP_DEEPENER_URL_CAP      60  citation-snowball deepener (run_honest_sweep_r3.py:3038)
434:    #   PG_R6_EXPAND_FETCH_CAP         40  R-6 completeness re-expansion (run_honest_sweep_r3.py:2961)
435:    #   PG_STORM_URL_FETCH_CAP         60  STORM web-results seed lane (I-beatboth-fix-000 BB-006)
436:    #   --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
437:    #   SUM                          1000  ≈ the ~1000-site/question budget (operator no-overshoot).
438:    #   I-beatboth-fix-000 (Codex P1): main lane trimmed 800->740 to ABSORB the new STORM seed lane so
439:    #   the total fetch stays at the hard 1000 envelope (no ~1060 overshoot).
440:    # NOTE: PG_STORM_MAX_BENCHMARK_QUERIES (30) and PG_MAX_SUBQUERIES (15) below are QUERY-BREADTH
441:    # counts (how many search queries are issued), NOT URLs — they are deliberately NOT part of the
442:    # ~1000-URL sum. .env has no override for any of these (checked I-fetch-002), so the floor lands.
443:    # Retrieval breadth — the REAL run_one_query knobs (PG_SWEEP_*, default 12/12/40). NOT PG_LIVE_*.
444:    "PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP": "740",   # MAIN lane: total URLs/query (lane 1/4); 800->740 to absorb STORM seed lane (1000 total)
445:    "PG_SWEEP_MAX_SERPER": "100",
446:    "PG_SWEEP_MAX_S2": "100",
447:    # FX-17 (#1126): Serper `num` is a PAGE size (max ~20); breadth needs the new PAGINATION budget.
448:    # Without these the benchmark stays single-page (~20/query) despite MAX_SERPER=100. 60 over <=3
449:    # pages = up to 3 Serper pages/query.
450:    "PG_SERPER_TOTAL_PER_QUERY": "60",
451:    "PG_SERPER_MAX_PAGES": "3",
452:    # Feature activation that Gate-B previously MISSED (STORM was dead-by-config; deepener off).
453:    "PG_STORM_ENABLED_IN_BENCHMARK": "1",
454:    "PG_SWEEP_EVIDENCE_DEEPENER": "1",
455:    # Observability — MUST be on so each feature's firing is provable in manifest['tool_utilization'].
960:# Codex diff-gate iter-2 P1-1: additional CALL-TIME env floors that .env was silently winning over.
961:_BENCHMARK_EXTRA_ENV_FLOORS = {
962:    "PG_MOST_MAX_EVIDENCE": 800,
963:    # I-ready-001 (#1070) P0 + operator decision 2026-06-10: fail closed if the generator-facing pool cap
964:    # is below the FULL extracted set — catches any regression that re-introduces a pool throttle (the

971:def apply_full_capability_benchmark_slate() -> None:
972:    """Make the full-capability slate AUTHORITATIVE over .env / conservative defaults (FLOOR semantics).
973:
974:    Codex diff-gate iter-2 P1-1: ``setdefault`` was WRONG. ``load_dotenv`` (openrouter_client import)
975:    puts .env values into ``os.environ`` BEFORE this slate runs, so a conservative .env default
976:    (e.g. ``PG_MOST_MAX_EVIDENCE=300``, ``PG_AGENTIC_WEB_PER_ROUND=6``) SURVIVED the setdefault and
977:    silently throttled the benchmark below the slate. Fix: every numeric key is a **FLOOR** —
978:    ``max(existing, slate)`` — so a HIGHER operator/.env value (more capability, e.g.
979:    ``PG_LLM_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=600`` in .env) is KEPT, but a LOWER default is RAISED to full capability.
980:    No silent downgrade in either direction (operator no-downgrade directive). Feature flags in
981:    ``_BENCHMARK_FORCE_ON_FLAGS`` are FORCED ON (a benchmark feature off is a capability downgrade).
982:    Exact-value flags in ``_BENCHMARK_FORCE_EXACT_FLAGS`` are forced to their slate value.
983:
984:    Codex diff-gate iter-2 P1-2: MUST run BEFORE the sweep / live_retriever / state imports, which cache
985:    ``PG_LIVE_CONTENT_MAX`` / ``PG_LIVE_HTTP_TIMEOUT`` / ``PG_AGENTIC_WEB_PER_ROUND`` as import-time module
986:    constants. ``main()`` applies it before ``load_locked_questions()``; ``run_gate_b_query`` applies it
987:    before the sweep import. ``preflight_full_capability`` then validates the LIVE module constants so a
988:    too-late application is caught fail-closed.
989:    """
990:    for name, value in _FULL_CAPABILITY_BENCHMARK_SLATE.items():
991:        if name in _BENCHMARK_FORCE_ON_FLAGS or name in _BENCHMARK_FORCE_EXACT_FLAGS:
992:            os.environ[name] = value                       # force exact value — no silent benchmark drift
993:            continue
994:        try:
995:            current = float(os.environ.get(name, value))
996:        except (TypeError, ValueError):
997:            current = float(value)
998:        os.environ[name] = str(int(max(current, float(value))))   # FLOOR: raise-to-slate, keep-if-higher
999:    # PG_MAX_COST_PER_RUN is an import-time constant in openrouter_client (cached before this slate via
1000:    # the role import chain), so the floor above only fixes the env; sync the live module global too so
1001:    # check_run_budget enforces the floored cap and run_one_query's manifest reads it (Codex iter-1 P1-2).
1002:    from src.polaris_graph.llm.openrouter_client import set_max_cost_per_run
1003:    set_max_cost_per_run(float(os.environ["PG_MAX_COST_PER_RUN"]))
1004:

1006:def preflight_full_capability() -> None:
1007:    """FAIL CLOSED if the effective benchmark config is below full capability or unobservable — so a
1008:    silent throttle (the ~40-URL bug) can NEVER reach a paid run undetected. Raises RuntimeError."""
1009:    for name, floor in _BENCHMARK_PREFLIGHT_FLOORS.items():
1010:        # mirror run_one_query's read of the real PG_SWEEP_* knob (defaults 12/12/40 if absent).
1011:        _defaults = {"PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP": "40", "PG_SWEEP_MAX_SERPER": "12", "PG_SWEEP_MAX_S2": "12"}
1012:        try:
1013:            eff = int(os.getenv(name, _defaults.get(name, "0")))
1014:        except ValueError:
1015:            raise RuntimeError(f"benchmark preflight: {name}={os.getenv(name)!r} is not an int")
1016:        if eff < floor:
1017:            raise RuntimeError(
1018:                f"benchmark preflight FAILED: {name}={eff} < full-capability floor {floor} — the run "
1019:                f"would be SILENTLY THROTTLED (the ~40-URL bug). Set {name}>={floor} or fix the slate."
1020:            )

3911:
3912:def _merge_bibliographies(
3913:    section_slices: list[list[dict[str, Any]]],
3914:) -> list[dict[str, Any]]:
3915:    """Merge per-section biblios into a single ordered bibliography,
3916:    remapping section-local citation numbers to global numbers."""
3917:    # Each section's biblio has its own 1-based numbering. We need to
3918:    # renumber globally, but the section's verified_text already has
3919:    # [1][2][3] markers in section-local space.
3920:    # Simpler approach: return the raw per-section biblios flattened,
3921:    # deduped by evidence_id, and let the caller remap the inline
3922:    # markers in a separate pass.
3923:    seen: dict[str, dict[str, Any]] = {}
3924:    for sl in section_slices:
3925:        for entry in sl:
3926:            ev_id = entry.get("evidence_id", "")
3927:            if ev_id and ev_id not in seen:
3928:                seen[ev_id] = dict(entry)
3929:    # Renumber globally
3930:    final: list[dict[str, Any]] = []
3931:    for i, entry in enumerate(seen.values(), 1):
3932:        new_entry = dict(entry)
3933:        new_entry["num"] = i
3934:        final.append(new_entry)
3935:    return final

1418:    else:
1419:        # LARGE-POOL PATH — bound the OUTLINE menu to the top-N highest-priority rows AND
1420:        # terse each digest (ev_id + tier + title only; DROP the 160-char statement). The
1421:        # pool is deterministically priority/tier/relevance-ORDERED upstream, so [:N] keeps
1422:        # exactly the rows sections prioritize and drops only the low-relevance tail. The
1423:        # statement text is unnecessary here because the outline only PLANS section
1424:        # structure; dropping it widens reasoning headroom at the same N, which is what
1425:        # prevents the reasoning-first writer from spending the whole completion ceiling on
1426:        # planning and emitting zero content (the drb_76 ReasoningFirstTruncationError).
1427:        # I-arch-002 (#1246) P-W4gen: under the redesign flag this terse digest covers the
1428:        # FULL pool (no [:N] truncation) — CONSOLIDATE-keep-all; OFF => the [:_outline_max_ev]
1429:        # menu slice, byte-identical.
1430:        outline_evidence = evidence if _outline_redesign else evidence[:_outline_max_ev]
1431:        summary_blocks = []
1432:        for ev in outline_evidence:
1433:            ev_id = ev.get("evidence_id", "")
1434:            title = (ev.get("title", "") or "")[:120]
1435:            tier = ev.get("tier", "")
1436:            title_clean, _ = sanitize_evidence_text(title)
1437:            if title_clean:
1438:                summary_blocks.append(f"{ev_id} [{tier}] | title: {title_clean}")
1439:            else:
1440:                summary_blocks.append(f"{ev_id} [{tier}]")
1441:        summary_text = "\n".join(summary_blocks)
1442:
1443:        prompt = (
1444:            f"Research question: {research_question}\n\n"
1445:            f"Evidence summaries ({len(outline_evidence)} rows):\n"
1446:            f"{summary_text}\n\n"
1447:            f"Return the JSON section plan."
1448:        )
1449:
1450:    # allowed_ev_ids stays on the FULL pool so outline validation does NOT regress: a section
1451:    # ev_id the LLM picks is accepted iff it is anywhere in the pool, and full-text resolution
1452:    # downstream (evidence_pool[ev_id]) spans every row. The cap shrank only the MENU, never
1453:    # the validation/resolution surface.
1454:    allowed_ev_ids = {ev.get("evidence_id", "") for ev in evidence}
1455:    allowed_ev_ids.discard("")
1456:
1457:    client = OpenRouterClient(model=model)
1458:    total_in = 0
1459:    total_out = 0
1460:    retry_attempted = False
1461:    try:
1462:        # I-gen-004 (#496): tag the outline call for the reasoning-trace sink.
1463:        set_reasoning_call_context(
1464:            section="_outline", call_type="outline", attempt_n=1,
1465:        )
1466:        response = await client.generate(
1467:            prompt=prompt,
1468:            system=_outline_system_prompt,
1469:            max_tokens=max_tokens,
1470:            temperature=temperature,
1471:        )
1472:        total_in += response.input_tokens
1473:        total_out += response.output_tokens
